State  Championships 

New  York  State  Championship. 

The  usual  attraction  the  New  York  State  Championship  meeting  has  had 
for  leading  players  throughout  the  country  was  evidenced  to  a  greater 
extent  than  ever  when  the  entries  closed  on  July  3.'. 
.  Eighty-eight  singles  asi)irants  and  by  far  the  fastest  doubles  teams  that 
were  brought  together  in  any  tournament  of  the  year  were  on  hand  when 
])lay   began   on   the   Crescent   club's   courts  at   Bay    Ridge,    August   2. 

The  singles  draw  was  a  splendid  one,  with  Bundy  and  Pell  the  leaders 
ill   one   half,  and   McLoughlin,   J'>ull  and   Mahan   the   "class"   in   the   other. 

The  doubles  division  was  not  so  even.  The  upper  half  contained  the 
champions,  Ilackett  and  Alexander,  Pell  and  Mahan,  Cardner  and  Long, 
and  McLoughlin  and  Bundy.  The  lower  had  Touchard  and  Little,  Bull 
and  Martin,  and  Church  and   Mathey. 

The  brst  round  resulted  in  some  excellent  matches,  the  best  of  which 
was  that  between  T.  K.  Pell  and  C.  R.  Gardner.  Pell  was  off  like  a  shot 
in  the  first  set,  which  he  won  at  6/1,  but  by  assiduous  attention  to 
'"Teddy's"  forehand,  Cardner  landed  the  second  at  6/4.  The  third  was 
close  up  to  three-all,  but  Gardner  erred  frequently  from  then  on,  and  Pell 
pulled  out  at  6/4.  The  later  preferred  to  remain  back  while  Gardner 
rushed  the  net  at  every  opportunity.  lie  was  brilliant  at  times,  but  at 
others  made  inexcusable  errors.  In  the  same  round  R.  IL  Palmer  had  the 
better    jf  a  slugging  bee  with   IL   L.   Westfall. 

The  second  round  there  was  nothing  to  warrant  attention,  but  the  third 
produced  some  excellent  tennis.  L.  E.  Mahan  engaged  H.  H.  Hackett  in 
an  interesting  aftair.  The  return  of  the  latter  to  singles  play  nearly  cost 
Malian  his  chances  right  there.  Ilackett  took  the  first  set,  6/4,  and  v.as 
within  a  point  of  the  second.  Mahan  stuck  it  cut,  however,  and  was 
rejiaid  by  an  easy  win  of  the  deciding  set.  Church  had  a  close  shave  in 
his  fight  with  H.  C.  Martin.  The  third  set  was  won  at  9/7.  Pell  out- 
classed Palmer,  for  the  latter  was  wild  as  a  deer.  I'ell  was  not  forced  to 
extend  himself  at  any  time.  F.  C.  Baggs,  a  player  of  mediocre  ability, 
created  a  big  sensation  by  taking  a  set  from  M.  H.  Long.  The  latter  was 
good  one  minute  and  bad  the  next,  but  he  so  far  outranked  Baggs  that  the 
latter  was  not  conceded  the  slightest  chance.  W.  M.  Hall  caught  young 
Washburn  on  a  bad  day  and  trounced  him  at  6/2,  6/2,  and  the  remaining 
favoiites  played  true  to  form. 

The  feature  of  the  fourth  round  was  the  Long-Liltle  meeting,  but  it  was 
a  short  aijd  decisive  victory  for  the  Easterner.  Long's  ground  strokes  were 
no  match  for  the  former's,  yet  he  persisted  in  playiiig  drive  for  drive  and 
rarely  attempted  to  gain  the  net.  L.itile's  play  was  sharp  and  true  and  he 
drove  perfectly  from  start  to  finish.  The  score  was  6/2,  6/3.  Pell  had 
his  hands  full  when  he  met  Hall,  narrowly  averting  a  defeat.  Hall's  rather 
slow,  high  bounding  drives  took  all  the  steam  out  of  Pell's  game,  and  it 
became  a  battle  of  lobs  or  "floaters"  which  threatened  to  be  interminable. 
At  the  eleventh  hour  Pell  began  to  hit  hard  and  the  effect  was  magical. 
He  passed   Hall  for  a  series   of  aces  and  took  the  deciding  set  at  9/7. 

A  feather  in  Mahan's  cap  was  his  defeat  of  the  19 10  champion,  F.  C. 
Inman.  He  accomplished  the  feat  in  straight  sets  by  sound  all-round  play 
and  a  remarkable  ne"  attack.  T.  C.  Bundy  started  off  in  careless  fashion 
in  his  match  with  H.  W.  Slocum.  At  5/1  against  l-.im  he  began  to  let  out, 
and  so  far  outclassed  .he  veteran  that  the  latter  did  not  win  another  game.

SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL.  101 

The  fifth  round  brought  out  two  fine  matches,  one  the  Little-Bundy  set-to, 
and  the  other  between  McLoughlin  and  Mahan. 

The  first  named  was  a  demonstration  of  ability  and  form  against  Simon- 
pure  generalship,  in  which  craft  emerged  triumphant.  Little  took  the  first 
set  at  8/6.  He  drove  and  volleyed  magnificently,  but  was  a  bit  slow  in 
covering  court.  The  defect  was  a  minor  one,  but  gave  -Bundy  an  object  of 
attack  which  he  worked  to  the  very  limit.  His  whole  game  was  one  long 
change  of  pace.  Short  chops,  deep  ones,  and  low,  deep  lobs  alternated 
evenly,  and  the  effect  gradually  became  apparent.  Little  was  forced  to 
cover  an  enormous  amount  of  ground  and  the  fatigue  of  such  necessity 
gradually  increased.  Toward  the  end  his  strokes  became  very  uncertain 
and  erratic  and  he  allowed  Bundy,  by  errors,  as  many  points  as  the  latter 
actually  earned. 

McLoughlin  evidently  had  underestimated  Mahan's  ability,  for  he  began  i 
their  match  with  some  very  careless  work.  When  he  did  steady  down  and 
try  his  utmost  it  was  too  late,  for  the  gigantic  New  Yorker  held  the  lead 
safe  for  the  set  at  7/5.  The  second  and  third  were  closer  than  the  score 
of  6/2,  6/3  indicates,  for  Mahan  was  dangerous  at  all  times.  In  the  third 
set  he  had  two  bad  slumps  in  which  he  dropped  his  service.  Had  he  main- 
tained the  high  standard  of  the  balance  of  his  play,  McLoughlin  might 
never  have  passed  on. 

Church  made  his  exit  after  his  encounter  with  Pell,  but  not  before  he 
had  given  his  older  rival  a  bad  scare.  He  swamped  the  latter  in  the  first 
set  and  made  a  strong  bid  for  the  third.  C.  M.  Bull,  Jr.,  was  the  remaining 
winner,   he   having  disposed  of  A.   B.   Wadsworth  at  6/4,   7/5. 

The  semi-final  matches,  which  were  the  best  of  five  sets,  were  both  played 
August   10. 

Bundy  and  Pell  were  the  principal  entertainers  and  had  the  championship 
court.  Bundy  led  off  with  a  3/1  lead,  but  Pell,  who  had  not  then  found 
his  gait,  suddenly  came  on,  winning  five  straight  games  and  the  first  set. 
Bundy  again  took  the  lead  and  this  time  managed  to  hold,  it,  winning 
at  6/4. 

The  third  set  was  Pell's  by  a  narrow  margin.  At  5/3  he  dropped  tw» 
games,  but  made  up  for  it  by  winning  the  following  two  and  his  second  set. 

The  fourth  was  exactly  like  the  first.  Bundy  started  well,  jgetting  to 
3/1  before  Pell  began  to  overhaul  him.  The  latter  drove  beautifully  and 
was  not  lacking  in  any  department  of  the  game.  He  duplicated  his  feat 
of  the  opening  set  and   ran  out  five   successive  games  and  the  match. 

On  the  adjoining  court  McLoughlin  and  Bull  were  engaging  in  a  very 
one-sided  battle.  It  was  Bull  who  had  put  the  Californian  out  of  the  run- 
ning in  the  same  event  a  year  ago  and  he  was  undergoing  the  disagreeable 
experience  of  his  opponent's  revenge.  Bull  was  outclassed  and  defeated 
from  beginning  to  end.      The   score   was  6/3,  6/3,  6/3. 

The  final  match  was  not  played  until  Monday,  August  14.  A  big  gallery- 
was  on  hand  in  the  hope  of  seeing  the  State  title  remain  in  a  New  Yorker's 
hands. 

McLoughlin  began  the  set  and  struck  his  stride  immediately.  Pell  won 
only  one  game  and  really  had  no  chance  to  get  started.  The  second  set  i 
was  a  corker.  Pell  began  to  gauge  the  Westerner's  shots  and  by  deep,  fast  \ 
driving  ran  up  to  5/2.  It  looked  like  his  set  then,  but  he  wavered  a  bit 
and  McLoughlin  came  on  with  a  great  burst  of  speed.  At  six-all,  however. 
Pell  forged  ahead  and  annexed  two  games  in  quick  succession.  McLoughlin 
worked  like  a  beaver  in  the  third  set  and  Pell  v.as  unable  to  stop  the 
fussilade  of  drives,  volleys  and  smashes  that  came  from  the  Californian's 
racket.  The  result  was  a  6/2  verdict  in  McLoughlin's  favor.  The  fourth 
set  was  nip  and  tuck  to  six-all.  Pell  had  repeated  chances  to  win,  but 
passed  them  up  time  after  time.  At  six-all  McLoughlin  shot  out  in  front 
and  won  the  set  and  match.  His  work  was,  on  the  whole,  better  than  it 
had  been  at  any  time  since  his  arrival  in  the  East.  He  volleyed  and 
smashed  with  great  severity  and  accuracy  and  his  driving  was  far  better 
than    it    had    previously    been.      His    service    lacked   a   bit    of    its    usual    tre- 


102  SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL. 

mendous  power,  but  was,  notwithstanding,  quite  as  effective,  for  it  was 
splendidly   placed. 

The  doubles  began  quietly  enough  with  the  exception  of  the  meeting  of 
Pell  and  Mahan  with  Long  and  Gardner.  The  first  set  w'ent  to  the  former 
pair  at  6,4.  In  the  second  they  led  at  2/0,  but  Long  and  Gardner  ran 
six  straight  games.  The  third,  played  in  fast  waning  light,  found  Long  at 
his  worst  and  Gardner  not  much  better.  Pell  and  Mahan  took  it  easily 
at  6/2. 

The  second  round  brought  together  Alexander  and  Hackett  and  O.  H. 
Hinck  and  IL  Torrence  The  latter  team  came  within  a  point  of  each  set, 
but  could  not  send  over  the  winning  shot.  Alexander  showed  how  badly 
in  need  of  practice  he  was  by  missing  many  shots  which  he  customarily 
kills,  and  Hackett,  though  better,  was  far  from  his  normal  form. 

in  tlie  fourth  round  Pell  and  Mahan  found  themselves  facing  the  cham- 
pions in  the  featured  match  of  the  day.  The  former  pair  started  carefully 
and  by  good,  sound  teiniis  took  the  tirst  set  at  6,  !;.  No  one  was  alarmed 
by  the  fact,  for  the  title  holders  were  often  in  apparently  bad  positions 
but  had  never  failed  to  pull  out.  But  when,  instead  of  living  up  to  their 
reputations,  they  dropped  game  after  game  until  six  had  been  played  and 
they  had  failed  to  win  one,  astonishment  was  unbounded.  Not  since  1907, 
in  which  year  they  tirst  won  the  national  championship,  had  they  tasted 
defeat,  and  it  without  elation  that  the  spectators  witnessed  their  clownfall. 
Pell  and  Mahan  had  played  faultlessly.  The  former  drove  for  ace  after 
ace  right  through  the  middle  of  his  opponent's  court  and  Mahan's  volleying 
was  nothing  short  of  miraculous.  His  enormous  reach  made  it  i)ossible  for 
him  to  return  and  kill  drives  that  looked  like  winners  and  his  great 
strength  made  it  easy  for  him  to  stop  with  ease  Alexander's  fastest  returns. 

Bull  and  Martin,  the  new  champions  of  the  West,  made  a  strong  bid  for 
the  opening  set  of  their  match  with  Little  and  Touchard,  but  the  second 
was  short  and  one-sided. 

The  meeting  of  the  western  pair.  Bundy  and  McLoughlin,  with  Pell  and 
Mahan  was  looked  forward  to  by  all  who  had  watched  both  teams  in  action, 
and  opinion  as  to  the  outcome   was  about  equally  divided. 

Ideal  conditions  existed  on  the  day  of  the  match  and  it  was  about  3 
o'clock  when  play  began. 

The  tirst  set  was  very  even,  but  at  six-all  the  New  Yorkers  fell  off  and 
were  distanced  in  the  succeeding  two  games.  The  second  set  was  all  in 
favor  of  the  Californians.  McLoughlin  was  a  tower  of  strength  on  all  his 
shots  and  it  was  largely  due  to  him  that  it  was  so  much  in  his  team's 
favor. 

Pell  and  Mahan  got  to  5/4  and  40/30  in  the  third  set,  but  the  following 
point,  a  smash  of  McLoughlin's,  tied  the  score,  and  they  were  never  dan- 
gerous from  then  on.  The  set  and  match  ended  v  hen  Peil,  in  an  attempt 
to   return  a  drive,   struck   Mahan  in   the  back  of   the   head. 

Mathey  and  Church  gave  Touchard  and  Little  a  hard  fight,  but  were 
outgeneraled  in  the  pinches.  Their  control  was  at  times  faulty,  whereas 
the  winners,  when  they  made  up  their  minds  to  play,  were  accurate  and 
fast.     The  score  was  3   6,  6   3,   7/5,  63. 

The  final,  played  August  i-.  was  watched  by  an  enormous  crowd.  Not 
an  inch  of  space  was  left  unoccupied  and  the  excitement  was  intense  from 
start  to  finish.  Touchard  began  the  match  with  service  but  could  not  get 
enough  pace  on  the  balls  to  win.  McLoughlin  followed,  but  he,  too.  proved 
ineffective,  and  the  score  was  one-all.  From  that  time  on  the  service  won, 
until  at  eleven-all  Bundy's  was  broken  through  and  Little  won  his  for 
the  set. 

The  second  set  was  another  terrific  fight  from  beginning  to  end.  At  5/6 
Bundy  just  squeezed  through  with  his  delivery  and  later,  at  g'lo.  Touchard 
and  Little  were  within  a  point  three  times,  again  oii  Bundy's  service.  It 
was  their  last  chance  for  the  set,  for  McLoughlin  broke  Touchard's  service 
a  game  later  and   won   tlie   set  with   his  own. 

The    third    and    fourth    sets    were    far    less   even,    but    furnished    a    higher 


srALDINGS    LAWN    TENNiS    ANNUAL.  103 

standard  of  play  on  Touchard's  and  Little's  part.  They  hit  harder  and 
with  even  greater  accuracy,  really  outclassing  their  opponents  as  a  team 
and  individuals.     The  scores  were  6/2  and  6/3.

Bi-State   Championship. 


At  the  Bi-State  championships,  held  by  the  Kentucky  Lawn  Tennis  Asso- 
ciation on  the  Audubon  courts  at  Louisville,  September  11  to  18,  R.  H. 
Palmer  took  the  singles  with  comparative  ease  by  defeating  Floyd  Day, 
6/3.  6/2,  6/2.  Clifford  Lockhorn  of  Cincinnati,  the  champion  of  19 10, 
had  to  be  content  with  sharing  the  honors  of  the  tournament  in  the  dou- 
bles when  he,  paired  with  Schaaf,  defeated  Palmer  and  Frank  in  the  best 
of   four  sets.      The   summary:

Tri-State  Championship. 


Richard  H.  Palmer  of  Ridgewood,  N.  J.,  successfully  defended  his  Tri- 
State  title  in  Cincinnati  on  September  9  against  Richard  Bishop  of  Boston, 
whom  he  defeated  in  straight  sets,  14/12,  6/4,  8/6.  Bishop  had  been  gen- 
erally selected  to  carry  off  the  honors  and  the  match  was  witnessed  by  tiie 
largest  gallery  of  the  tournament.  In  the  doubles  Bishop  and  Hen/y  C. 
Johnson,  another  Bostonian,  won  from  Nat  Emerson  and  W.  M.  Hall,  who 
were  defeated  in  the  best  of  four  sets.     The  summary:

New  Jersey  State  Championship. 

C.  K.  F.  Andrews,  an  English  player  who  was  defeated  at  Newport  by 
Beals  C.  Wright,  won  the  New  Jersey  State  Championship  on  the  courts 
of  the  Morristown  Field  Club,  September  i6,  when  he  defeated  Wylie  C. 
Grant  in  the  final  round.  The  score  was  6/4,  6/-2,  1/6,  6/2.  Mrs.  Mar- 
shall McLean  and  R.  D.  Little  won  the  mixed  doubles  from  Mrs.  Edgar 
and  Lindsay  Dunham  in  the  final  round  in  straight  sets,  and  Mrs.  McLean 
defeated  Miss  Bunce  in  the  singles,  6/4,  6/2.     The  summary:

Maryland  State  Championship. 

Owing  to  the  fact  that  no  players  of  rank  competed,  the  annual  tour- 
nament for  the  championship  of  Maryland  proved  somewhat  disappointing, 
the  event  resolving  itself  into  a  purely  local  aifair.  In  the  final  round 
Fisher  and  Wagner,  two  old  rivals,  met  and  furnished  the  best  play  of 
the  tournament.  Fisher,  a  much  improved  player,  was  too  fast  for  his 
heavy  rival,  his  better  condition  at  the  beginning  of  the  fifth  set  allowing 
a  comparatively  easy  win.  The  title  holder,  R.  A.  Holden,  Jr..  did  not 
defend.      The    summary:

Oregon  State  Championship. 

On  July  17  the  tournament  for  the  championship  of  Oregon  began  at 
the  Multnomah  Amateur  Athletic  Club  of  Portland.  The  entry  of  Nat 
Emerson  and  C.  E.  Foley,  a  San  Franciscan  of  well  known  ability, 
enhanced  the  interest  of  the  meeting  greatly.  The  latter  had  no  trouble 
in  reaching  the  final  round.  He  disposed  of  Wickersham,  one  of  the  best 
local   men,   easily,  and   in   the   final   won   from    Shives   at   6/1,   6/2,   3/6,   6/3. 

Emerson,  in  his  attempt  to  defend  his  title  against  Foley,  showed  how 
badly  in  need  of  practice  he  was.  As  a  player  he  was  a  shadow  of  his 
former  self.  He  won  the  first  set,  6/3,  but  thereafter  had  never  a  chance. 
Foley   won  at  6/1.  6/3,   6/1. 

The  doubles  went  to  Foley  and  J.  W.  Lewis,  a  local  man  of  fair  ability. 
It  was  generally  expected  that  Gorrill  and  Wickersham,  who  had  won  the 
North  Pacific  International  a  week  earlier,  would  have  things  their  own 
way,   but  they  were  defeated,   6/1,   3/6,   6/1,   6/3.     The   summaries: 

Colorado  State  Championship. 

W.  L.  Andrews,  Jr.,  is  the  191 1  champion  of  Colorado,  having  won  that: 
title  on  the  courts  of  the  Denver  Country  Club,  by  the  defeat  of  A.  G. 
McKay  in  the  final  round  at  4/6,  6/3,  6/3,  6/3.  The  event  was  started^, 
on  August  28  and  completed  the  following  Saturday.  Dan  Harker  and 
T.  B.  Townsend,  Jr.,  won  the  doubles,  defeating  Hughes  and  Andrews  iu 
the   final    match. 

In  coming  through  the  singles  Andrews  lost  a  set  to  D.  B.  Knowlton  ir. 
the  first  round,  winning  6/2,  2/6,  6/3.  McKay  had  a  hard  time  witb 
Townsend  in  the  semi-final  round,  winning  0/6,  6/3,  7/5,  6/0. 

Harker    and    Townsend    had    two    close    matches    in    winning   the    doubles,, 
several  of  the  teams  being   pretty  evenly  matched.      The   summaries:

Virginia  State  Championship. 

T.  R.  Pell,  the  well  known  expert  from  New  York,  took  a  spring  trip 
and  as  a  souvenir  of  his  journey  brought  back  to  Gotham  the  Virginia 
State  championship  title,  along  with  several  others.  The  meeting  was  held 
at  the  Norfolk  Country  Club  in  June,  and  though  small  in  numbers,  was 
a  "classy"  event,  indeed.  Pell  had  a  rather  easy  time  in  coming  through, 
although  J.   S.  Taylor   made   him   play  an  odd  set  in   an   early   round. 

The  final  against  H.  Whitehead  proved  a  walkover  for  the  New  Yorker. 
He  won  as  he  chose  at  6/3,  6/1,  6/2.  The  Virginian  was  far  below  his 
average  standard,  which,  of  course,  accounted  for  the  severity  of  his 
defeat.  Against  Pell,  J.  H.  Winston,  the  champion,  did  much  better  than 
any  of  "Teddy's"  other  opponents  were  able  to  do.  The  Southerner,  by 
clever  net  play,  took  the  first  set  at  6/2,  but  Pell  won  the  follov/ing 
through,   the   last   of   which   was   6/0. 

Pell  paired  with  T.  R.  Bogert  in  the  doubles,  and  though  they  won  the 
tournament,  they  were  soundly  whioned  in  straight  sets  by  Whitehead  and 
Winston   in   the   challenge   round.      The    summaries:

Delaware  State  Championship. 

Seeking  new  fields  to  conquer,  C.  R.  Gardner  of  New  York  took  train 
to  Wilmington,  Del.,  and  there,  after  a  series  of  hard  and  easy  matches, 
wrested  the  title  of  State  champion  from  W.  F.  Johnson.  The  tourna- 
ment was   held  at  the   Wilmington   Country  Club,  and   began  June   26. 

Gardner  came  through  his  half  of  the  draw  easily  enough,  and  F.  C. 
Inman,  another  expert  of  the  Metropolitan  district,  had  an  equally  easy 
time.  Their  meeting  in  the  final  was  the  best  of  the  week  and  went  to 
four  sets.  Inman  took  the  first  at  6/4,  but  Gardner,  by  splendid  net  play 
and  the  aid  of  a  fast,  sliding  chop,  took  the  following  three  at  6/2,  6/1, 
6/3,  respectively.  Inman  seemed  unable  to  do  anything  with  Gardner's 
twisting  ground  strokes,  and  his  usually  effective  driving  was  noticeable 
for  its  absence. 

In  the  challenge  round  against  Johnson,  Gardner  was  at  his  best.  In 
spite  of  intense  heat,  he  worked  hard  for  every  point.  The  first  set  went 
to  him  at  6/2  and  the  second  at  9/7.  The  third  was  much  slower,  but 
what  bursts  of  speed  appeared  were  all  the  New  Yorker's,  and  he  ran  out 
at  6/4.     Johnson  was,   as  usual,   deadly  with  a  forehand  chop,   but  his  back- 


116  SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL. 

hand  was  not  up  to  the  mark.  It  was  by  placing  deep  shots  to  Johnson's 
backhand  and  running  in  to  kill  the  return  that  Gardner  won  as  easily 
as   he   did. 

The  doubles  went  to  Inman  and  A.  Holmes  without  a  set  being  won 
from  them.  They  outclassed  every  team  that  went  against  them,  including 
the  title-holders,  H.  M.   Tilden  and  A.  Thayer.      The  summaries:

District  of  Columbia  Championship. 

R.  L.  James  sprang  into  sudden  prominence  in  Washington  tennis  cir- 
cles when,  in  May,  he  won  the  championship  of  the  District  of  Columbia. 
James  came  throUt,h  one  half  and  C.  B.  Doyle  the  other.  Then,  for  a 
reason   not  clearly   understood,    Doyle   defaulted   to   James,   and   his   brother.

H.  E.  Doyle,  did  likewise  in  the  challenge  round.  James  had  the  cham- 
pion two  sets  down  when  the  latter  withdrew,  and  it  is  more  than  likely 
that  the   title  would   have  passed   from  him,   regardless  of  his  default.

Pennsylvania  State  Championship. 

Philadelphia  lias  for  many  years  produced  the  player  to  win  the  Penn- 
sylvania State  championship,  but  191 1  proved  the  year  of  Pittsburgh's  suc- 
cessful invasion,  when  P.  D.  Siverd,  a  player  who  has  improved  remarkably 
in   two   short   seasons,   took   the   title   away   from   Wallace   F.   Johnson. 

The  meeting  began  on  June  5  at  the  Merion  Cricket  Club  of  Haverford. 
Siverd  in  winning  exhibited  splendid  form,  defeating,  in  succession,  F.  C. 
Inman  and  R.  H.  Palmer,  and  in  the  final  round  F.  G.  Anderson.  Johnson 
was  no  match  for  the  Smoky  City  champion  and  lost  his  title  and  the 
challenge  match  at  8/6,   9/7,   6/2. 

The  doubles  title  also  changed  hands,  when  H.  M.  Tilden  and  A.  D. 
Thayer  downed  J.  R.  Carpenter,  Jr.  and  E.  B.  Dewhurst.  The  younger 
team  had  a  wide  margin  at  the  end  of  each  set,  except  the  second,  which 
Carpenter  and  Dewhurst  won  at    10/8.     The  summaries: 

MEN'S   SINGLES.

Siverd    d.   R.    H.    Palmer,   6/3,   6/3. 

Final   round — P.    D.   Siverd   d.   F.   G.   Anderson,   6/3,   6/4.   6/2. 
Challenge    round— P.    D.    Siverd    d.   W.    F.    Johnson,    8/6,   9/7,    6/1.

Idaho  State  Championship. 

On  June  14  the  championship  of  the  State  of  Idaho  began  at  the  Lewis- 
ton  Tennis  Club  of  Lewiston.  There  was  a  stronger  entry  than  usual,  but 
T.  C.  Fulton  led  the  field  from  beginning  to  end.  The  newcomer  was 
victorious  over  J.  C.  Tyler,  the  Washington  expert,  in  the  semi-final,  at 
6/3,  8/6.  7/5,  and  won  hands  down  from  the  191  o  champion,  ^iray.  Tyler 
and  Fulton  outclassed  the  balance  of  the  doubles  field,  winning  the  tour- 
nament without  the  loss  of  a  set.     The  summaries:

New  Hampshire  State  Championship. 

The  sixth  annual  championship  of  New  Hampshire,  played  on  the  Craw- 
ford House  courts  in  the  White  Mountains,  July  31  and  following  days, 
was  won  by  F.  H.  Harris  of  Brattleboro,  Vt.,  in  the  singles,  and  by  Harris 
and  J.  T.  Nelson  in  the  doubles.  W.  B.  Cragin,  Jr.,  reached  the  final 
round  of  the  singles,  where  he  was  put  out  by  L.  H.  Martin.  Later  Martin 
fell   before   Harris  in  the   challenge   round.     The   summaries:

Wyoming  State  Championship. 

W.  C.  Snow  is  still  the  champion  01  Wyoming,  having  successfully 
defended  his  title  against  Hamilton,  the  tournament  winner,  and  thus  gain- 
ing his  second  leg  on  the  challenge  cup.  The  tournament  was  postponed 
from  July  17,  being  held  Friday,  Saturday  and  Monday,  September  22,  23 
and  25,  at  Basin,  Wyo.  Fourteen  players  entered  the  singles  and  four 
teams  played  for  the  doubles,  which  event  went  to  Snow  and  Nowell,  who 
defeated  Hamilton  and  Johnson,  6/3.  6/0,  8/6,  in  the  final  round.  The 
boy's  tournament  was  won  by  Julian  Snow,  who  defeated  Rupert  Ander- 
son, 1/6,  6/3,  6/3,  in  the  final.  Each  finalist  had  previously  won  a  three- 
set  match.  Snow  defeating  Adrian  Smith,  4/6,  6/2,  7/5,  while  Anderson 
defeated   Harris,   9/7,   4/6,   6/7.      The   summaries: 

MEN'S  SINGLES. 

First  round— Hamilton  d.  Johnson,  6/3,  8/6;  Higby  d.  Tallon.  by 
default;  Bishop  d.  Sizer.  2/6,  6/4,  6/3;  Howell  d.  Lewis  Zimmerman,  6/3, 
6/4;   Hunter  d.   Howell,   7/5,  6/1;    H.   Harris  d.   Norris,   6/2,   6/0. 

Second  round — Hamilton  d.  Hart,  by  default;  Bishop  d.  Higby,  6/3, 
6/1;   Hunter   d.   Howell,   6/0,   9/7;    H.   Harris  d.    G.   Harris,  by   default. 

Third  round— Hamilton  d.  Bishop,  6/2,  6/1;  H.  Harris  d.  Hunter,  by 
default. 

Final   round— Hamilton   d.    H.    Harris,   6/1,    7/5- 

Challenge  round — W.   C.    Snow   (champion)   d.   Hamilton,  6/1,   7/9,   6/1.

West  Virginia  State  Championship. 

The  sixth  annual  invitation  tennis  tournament  for  the  championship  of 
West  Virginia  was  held  on  the  courts  of  the  Parkersburg  Country  Club, 
August  21,  22  and  23,  191 1.  Each  succeeding  year  seems  to  be  more  pro- 
ductive of  interest  and  enthusiasm  than  its  predecessor  and  the  splendid 
entry  list,  together  with  ideal  weather  and  high  class  tennis,  made  this 
tournament  the  most  successful  one  in  the  history  of  the  club.  Besides 
the  numerous  informal  affairs  arranged  for  the  visiting  players,  they  were 
royally  entertained  on  the  evening  of  the  second  day  at  a  large  banquet, 
and  the  brilliant  club  dance  on  the  evening  of  the  third  day  marked  a 
fitting  close  of  the  tennis  season.  In  the  singles  event  the  championship 
was  carried  away  by  Everett  Drennen  of  Fairmont,  W.  Va.,  who  success- 
fully defended  in  the  challenge  round  against  Phil  Laughlin  of  Wheeling, 
and  by  his  finished  and  aggressive  play  won  in  straight  sets  by  a  score  of 
6/4.  6/3,  6/2.  However,  great  credit  is  due  to  Mr.  Laughlin  for  his  clever 
and  consistent  play  throughout  the  tournament  and  it  made  quite  an 
impression  among  the  followers  of  the  game.  The  doubles  championship 
was  won  by  R.  A.  Johnson  and  J.  A.  Shrewsbury  of  Parkersburg  against 
Messrs.  Washington  and  Lawrence  of  Charleston.  The  tennis  committee 
consists  of  R.  A.  Johnson,  chairman;  J.  A.   Shrewsbury  and  E.   R.  Kingsley.

Illinois  State  Championship. 

Walter  T.  Hayes  strengthened  his  claim  to  recognition  as  th*  strongest 
player  of  the  Middle  West,  when,  in  August,  he  successfully  defended  his 
title  of  Illinois  champion  against  his  challenger,  Albrecht  Ludke.  The 
event  was  held  on  the  turf  courts  of  the  Aztec  Tennis  Club  (ni  Chicago. 
The  entry  was  a  record-breaker  and  included  -all  the  best  men  of  that 
section  of  the  country.  In  the  first  round  W.  Wilkens  upset  Heath 
Byford.  The  latter,  one  of  Chicago's  best  men,  was  a  bit  off  his  stroke 
and  Wilkens,  who  is  famous  for  his  hard  hitting,  won  easily  at  6/2,  6/3. 
Ludke  and  Wilkes,  old  rivals,  met  in  the  third  round  and,  contrary  to 
expectations,  Ludke  won  in  two  sets.  The  semi-final  brought  together 
Ludke  and  C.  C.  Collier  and  C.   S.  Peters  against  E.  Morley.     The  results 


128  SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL. 

were  quick  wins  by  Ludke  and  Peters.  They  outclassed  their  respective 
opponents   and  both    won   in   straight   sets. 

The  final  was  disappointing.  In  19 lo  Ludke  and  Peters  had  a  great 
match,  but  the  meeting  in  question  was  slow  and  uninteresting.  Peters 
was  no  match  for  the  German  expert  and  lost  at  6/3,  6/3,  6/2.  Morley 
and  Ludke  won  the  doubles.  Their  hardest  match  was  in  the  semi-final 
where  they  faced  Hayes  and  Peters,  but  even  the  latter  two  could  not 
press   them   very   hard. 

Miss  Carrie  B.  Neely  won  the  women's  singles,  defeating  Miss  Edith 
Paradise  in  the  final,  and  taking  the  title  by  default  from  Miss  Miriam 
Steever,  who  was  in  Europe  at  that  time.     The  summaries:

North  Dakota  State  Championship. 

North  Dakota  held  its  championship  during  the  week  of  July  10  at  the 
Town  and  Country  Club  of  Grand  Forks.  As  usual  the  Red  River  Valley 
championship  was  run  off  in  conjunction  with  the  State  meeting,  and  ended 
in  the  defeat  of  the  champion,  E.  S.  Read,  by  F.  W.  Leistikow  of  Win- 
nipeg. An  unusual  score  was  recorded,  for  although  the  match  went  five 
sets  Leistikow  won  three  at  love.  The  score  was  6/0,  3/6,  3/6,  6/0,  6/0. 
Mayes  and  Leistikow  won  the  doubles  from  Elton  and  Willson  at  6/4, 
5/7,    6/3. 

The  State  tournament  resulted  in  a  victory  for  F.  Willson.  He  defeated 
Dr.  Blatherwick,   6/0,   6/4,    5/7,    6/8,   6/3. 

Blatherwick  and  Sunberg  captured  the  doubles,  winning  from  Russ  and 
Phelps  in  the  final   at  6/4,  6/3,  6/0.     The  summaries:

Rhode  Island  State  Championship. 

The  annual  championship  for  the  State  of  Rhode  Island  came  to  an  end 
late  in  June.  E.  T.  Gross,  for  years  one  of  the  State's  top-notchers, 
annexed  the  championship  in  both  singles  and  doubles.  Gross  played  with 
J.  D.  E.  Jones  in  doubles  and  the  two  outclassed  all  the  teams  they  faced. 
In  singles  J.  O.  Ames  fought  out  the  final  round  with  Gross,  but  after 
winning    the    opening    set    was    outplayed    completely.      The    summaries:

Massachusetts  State  Champiohship. 

Next  to  Beals  Wright,  N.  W.  Niles  is  probably  the  best  player  in 
Massachusetts,  and  that  the  State  title  should  fall  to  him  again  is  as  it 
should  be.  He  did  not  prove  his  superiority  very  decisively,  however,  and 
for  a  time  it  looked  very  much  as  though  his  laurels  were  on  the  verge 
3f  departing,  for  that  sturdy  little  veteran,  F.  J.  Sulloway,  forced  him  to 
a  very   close  five-set   match   in  the   challenge   round. 

The  tournament  is  decided  at  a  time,  June  10,  when  few  players  are  in 
good  form.  Longwood  was  the  battle-ground  as  usual,  and  the  entry  was 
substantially   the   same   that   it   had   been   for   years. 

The  surprise  of  the  meeting  was  E.  T.  Dana's  first  round  with  Har- 
vard's champion,  E.  H.  Whitney.  The  latter  was  in  anything  but  top 
form,  and  the  steady  get-back  game  played  by   Dana  won  out. 

The  fifth  round,  in  which  four  matches  were  scheduled,  was  marred 
by  three  defaults.  In  the  only  match  that  was  played  Sulloway  defeated 
A.    S.   Dabney,  Jr.,  in  two  sets  at  6/4,  6/0. 

The  semi-final  resulted  in  Dick  Bishop's  win  from  H,  I.  Forster  and 
SuUoway's  crushing  defeat  of  Dana,  in  which  the  latter  won  but  two 
games.  Bishop  looked  as  though  he  might  get  away  with  Sulloway  in 
the  final,  but  after  winning  the  first  set  was  outplayed  completely.  Sullo- 
way won  at  4/6,   7/5,   6/2,   6/3. 

In  the  challenge  round  Niles  was  very  erratic.  He  came  in  constantly, 
but  between  passing  and  volleying  poorly  made  little  headway.  Sullo- 
way won  the  first  set  at  io/8  and  the  third  6/3.  The  fourth  and  fifth 
were  faster  and  saw  Niles  much  improved.  He  had  better  control  and 
volleyed  short  and  at  sharp  angles.  Sulloway  covered  Niles  in  going  for 
the  ball,  but  his  earnestness  got  him  nothing  in  the  end.  The  score  was 
8/10,   6/4,   3/6,  6/2,  6/2.     The   summaries:

Massachusetts  State  Doubles. 

The  tennis  season  in  Boston  was  ushered  in  by  the  tournament  for  the 
State  champion  of  Massachusetts,  which  was  played  at  the  Brae  Burn 
Club.  B.  C.  Wright  and  F.  J.  Sulloway  renewed  their  partnership  and 
had  little  trouble  in  winning  the  tournament.  In  the  final,  Seaver  and 
Putnam  were  downed  in  four  sets,  but  the  defending  pair,  Niles  and  Dab- 
ney, were  even  easier  for  the  challenging  team.  Wright  and  Sulloway 
were  much  the  faster,   winning  at  6/4,  6/2,  6/3.     The  summaries:

Texas  State  Championship. 

Semp  Russ  proved  the  fallacy  of  the  "can't  come  back"  theory  on  June 
19,  when  at  the  San  Antonio  Country  Club  he  regained  the  ■  Texas  State 
title  and  dethroned  no  less  a  person  than  H.  M.  McQuiston.  The  match 
which  placed  Russ  on  the  tennis  map  for  the  second  time  was  an  interesting 
five-set  affair.  McQuiston  held  his  own  for  four  sets,  but  in  the  fifth  his 
opponent's  sl'illful  net  work  was  too  much  for  him  and  he  scored  only  a 
single    game. 

Russ  played  with  Walthall  in  the  doubles  and  there  again  he  proved  his 
class.  McQuiston  and  Payne  made  a  bid  for  the  title,  but  the  rock  in  the 
road  bobbed  up  in  Russ  and  his  partner  in  the  final  round  and  they  were 
defeated  at   6/1,    7/5,    5/7,   6/1.      The    summaries:

Florida  State  Championship. 

On  February  24  Percy  Siverd  annexed  the  third  annual  State  cham- 
pionship of  Florida,  which  is  played  on  the  courts  of  the  Royal  Poinciana 
Hotel  at  Palm  Beach,  neither  B.  Wright,  who  won  the  event  in  1910,  nor 
G.  M.  Church,  who  succeeded  him  the  following  year,  were  on  hand,  and 
the  result  was  a  meeting  in  the  final  between  Siverd  and  A,  S.  Dabney  of 
Boston,   to  settle  the  holding  of  the  State  title. 

There  were  a  number  of  good  men  entered  and,  next  to  the  finalist,, 
young  Ralph  Racey,  a  local  player,  showed  greater  ability  than  the  balance 
of  the  field.  He  forced  Siverd  to  a  close  three-set  match,  in  which  he 
won  the  first  set,  6/4,  and  lost  the  following  two  by  the  same  score. 
Siverd  scored  his  victory  over  Dabney  in  the  final  at  6/4,  6/4,  0/6,  6/3, 
Rendall  and  Siverd  defeated  Dabney  and  Reece  in  the  finals  of  the  doubles 
quite  easily  at  6/0,  6/2,  6/3.     The  summaries:

California  State  Championship. 

The  eleventh  annual  championship  for  the  State  of  California  began  on 
November  29  on  the  University  of  California  courts  at  Berkeley.  While 
the  entry  was  not  a  big  one,  it  was  sprinkled  with  players  of  national 
reputation.  Herbert  Long,  brother  of  the  young  internationalist,  won  the 
singles,  but  had  the  time  of  his  life  in  disposing  of  B.  H.  Batkin  It  was 
only  the  former's  beautiful  dribbing  that  enabled  him  to  pull  out  the  third 
set  at  9/7.  The  challenge  round  between  Herbert  and  Melville  Long  was 
^T  ,,  M^,'^,^^  r^"^'^'.'^^'^^'^^^'  though  interesting  while  it  lasted,  was  much  in 
Mellville  s  favor  from  start  to  finish.  The  brothers  have  played  together 
so  often  that  each  is  aware  of  the  other's  limitations  and  it  was  Melville's 
greater  versatility  that  gave  him  such  a  big  advantage  over  his  more 
methodical    brother. 

C.  F;oley  and  Herbert  Long  won  the  doubles,  defeating  Berry  and 
Lvans  in  the  semi-final  in  straight  sets  and  Reuben  Hunt  and  J.  C.  Rohlis 
w  /  r.^  by  the  one-sided  score  of  6/1,  6/3,  6/3.  Melville  Long  and 
Ward  Dawson  defaulted  their  title  to  Foley  and  Long  in  the  challenge 
round.  Mrs.  Aiemeyer  challenged  Miss  Hazel  Hotchkiss  for  the  title  but 
was  repulsed  without  great  effort  on  the  champion's  part  at  6/2.  6/2  The 
summaries:  /    -     /

Montana  State  Championship. 

The  Montana  State  championship  was  held  for  the  third  time  at  the 
Hunter's  Hot  Springs  Hotel  on  August  14  and  following  days.  Dr  Alfred 
Karsted  of  Butte  won  the  singles  event,  defeating  McLeod  in  the  final 
round  6/3,  6/1,  6/2.  McLaughlin,  the  sixty-year-old  expert,  who  had  held 
the  title  or  several  years  past,  was  not  up  to  his  form  of  the  season  betore 
and  lost  to  McLeod  at  6/3,  6/2,  in  the  second  round.  The  summaries:

Michigan  State  Championship. 

A  new  champion  was  created  when  Richard  H.  Doughty  annexed  the 
championship  singles  from  Charles  O.  Benton,  of  Cleveland,  Ohio,  the 
previous  holder  of  the  Michigan  title,  in  straight  sets.  Doughty  is  a  new- 
comer in  Michigan  tennis  and  there  is  apparently  no  doubt  of  hs  superi- 
ority to  most  if  not  all  of  the  State  experts.  Playing  with  Ford,  whom 
he  had  defeated  in  the  final  of  the  singles,  Doughty  won  the  doubles  cham- 
pionship from  Corey  and  Leidy.  The  match  was  a  close  one,  three  of  the 
four  sets  played  going  to  deuce.  The  event,  which  began  on  August  28, 
was  successful  from  every  standpoint  and  was  by  far  the  biggest  which 
had  ever  been   played  off  in  Detroit.

Wisconsin  State  Championship. 

The  twenty-fourth  annual  tournament  for  the  championship  of  Wisconsin 
was  begun  on  August  5  at  the  Town  Club  of  Milwaukee.  A.  M.  Squair, 
a  Chicago  University  freshman,  won  the  tournament  and  then  challenged 
and  defeated  the  title  holder,  J.  I.  B.  Larned,  in  a  splendidly  contested 
five-set  match.  Larned,  however,  had  better  luck  in  the  doubles,  for, 
playing  with  J.  J.  Forstall,  he  successfully  defeated  his  title  against  G.  B. 
Wilson  and  R.  O.  Friend.  The  challenging  team  failed  to  score  a  set 
against  the  champions,  who  won  at  6/3,  6/3,   6/3.     The  summaries:

Oklahoma  State  Championship. 

Fifty-two  entries  in  singles  and  twenty-four  doubles  teams  broke  all 
records  for  the  Oklahoma  State  championship,  which  began  August  22. 
Charles  Speice  met  and  defeated  Harry  Southard  in  the  final  round  of  the 
singles.  Southard  got  off  well,  winning  the  first  set  at  6/2,  but  the  set- 
back acted  as  a  tonic  on  Speice,  who  came  on  with  a  rush  and  won  at 
6/3,    6/2,   6/2. 

Speice  and  his  partner,  John  G.  Bailey,  were  much  too  fast  for  Southard 
and  Fleming,  whom  they  met  in  the   doubles.     The  summaries:

Tennessee  State  Championship. 

B.  E.  Cornelius  of  Memphis  displaced  Champion  Cowan  Rodgers  in  the 
■challenge  round  of  the  Tennessee  State  championship  tournament,  which 
was  begun  on  June  26  at  the  Memphis  Tennis  Club.  Cornelius  took  his 
title  by  default,  but  in  winning  the  tournament  proved  his  right  to  bear 
the  burden  of  a  State's  premier  honors.  He  had  several  close  matches, 
but  none  to  compare  with  his  five-set  battle  against  W.  C.  Alexander  in 
the  final  round.  The  latter  won  two  of  the  first  three  sets  and  was  within 
•a  few  points  of  the  fourth.  The  fifth  was  close,  but  went  to  Cornelius  at 
6/4.  Ehlers  and  Cornelius  won  the  doubles  tournament,  but  lost  the 
challenge  round  to  the  title  holders,  Hardy  and  Cooper,  in  a  close  five-set 
affair.     The  summaries:

Indiana  State  Championship. 

The  tournament  for  the  State  championship  of  Indiana,  which  was  held 
at  Indianapolis  on  August  29  and  following  days,  was  the  most  successful 
ever  held  in  that  State.  The  standard  of  play  was  much  improved  over 
that  of  previous  years  and  the  entry  list  comprised  many  players  of 
ability  from  various  sections  of  the  State.  The  singles  event  was  won  by 
Wentzell.  His  opponent  in  the  final  was  H.  Anthony  of  Muncie  and 
though  the  match  went  to  five  sets  Wentzell  proved  his  superiority  by 
winning  the  fifth  at  love.  Brodix  and  Anthony,  playing  together  in 
doubles,   won  from  Appall  and  Trask  in  the  final  at  4/6,   6/4,  7/5,  6/3.

Connecticut  State  Championship. 

F.  C.  Inman  retained  his  title  of  Connecticut  State  champion  in  spite 
of  C.  L.  Johnston's  efforts  to  take  it  from  him.  As  usual,  the  tournament 
was  played  at  the  Litchfield  Club  the  week  of  July  10.  Johnston  came 
through  the  singles  in  good  style,  although  he  had  a  close  match  with  Dr. 
P.  B.  Hawk,  in  the  semi-final  and  another  in  the  final  with  young  Vander- 
bilt  Ward.  He  defeated  Hawk  7/5,  8/6,  and  Ward  2/6,  6/3,  6/4,  8/6. 
Against  Inman  Johnston,  though  he  won  the  second  set  at  11/9,  failed  to 
make  much  headway.  The  latter's  hard  drives  and  service  made  big  holes 
through  the  Amherst  player's  court  and  he  won  three  sets  fairly  easily  at 
6/3,  6/3,  6/2.  F.  M.  Watrous  and  W.  S.  Anderson  won  the  doubles,  defeat- 
ing Dr.  Hawk  and  C.  A.  Lindley  in  the  final  at  4/6,  7/5,  10/8,  6/2.  The 
summaries:

Iowa  State  Championship. 


The  sixth  annual  tournament  for  the  Iowa  State  championship  was  held 
on  the  Golf  and  Country  Club  courts  of  Des  Moines,  commencing  August 
14.  R.  L.  Branson  of  South  Dakota  won  the  tournament  and  challenged 
F.  W.  Bradley  for  the  latter's  title  and  defeated  him  in  three  straight 
sets,  6/4,  6/3,  6/3.  Oilman  and  Carey,  the  19 10  doubles  holders,  were 
unable  to  defend  their  title  and  it  thus  passed  to  Branson  and  Young. 
The  principal  match  of  the  week  was  that  between  Branson  and  Hoerr  in 
the  final  round.  It  was  a  great  contest,  as  close  as  one  could  wish  to  see. 
Branson   won    13/11,   7/9,   6/3,   8/6.     The   summaries:

Washington  State  Championship. 

Seattle  was  again  the  scene  of  the  annual  championship  of  the  State  of 
Washington,  which  began  on  August  15.  A  number  of  players  from  other 
States  competed,  among  them  being  Captain  J.  F.  Foulkes  of  Victoria. 
Joe  Tyler  of  Spokane  won  the  singles,  his  opponent  in  the  final  round 
being  L.  K.  Richardson.  Richardson  was  outclassed  and  lost,  6/2,  6/2,  6/3. 
In  the  doubles  Tyler  paired  up  with  Foulkes  and  together  they  proved 
too   strong  a    combination    for    Russell   and    Smith.      The    summaries:

Minnesota  State  Championship. 

On  August  19,  at  Duluth,  J.  J.  Armstrong  and  J.  W.  Adams,  both  of 
St.  Paul,  met  in  the  challenge  round  of  the  tournament  for  the  State 
championship  and  the  former  won  in  straight  sets.  Armstrong  previously 
held  the  title  in  1909.  Adams  had  taken  it  from  him  in  191  o  and  it  was 
generally  thought  that  he  would  succeed  in  retaining  it.  It  was  therefore 
with  considerable  surprise  that  the  spectators  saw  little  Armstrong  com- 
pletely outclass  his  old-time  rival.  Armstrong  in  coming  through  the 
tournament  did  not  lose  a  set  and  his  playing  from  the  first  day  on  was 
such  an  improvement  over  his  performances  of  a  year  ago  that  it  was 
remarkable.  In  the  final  of  the  doubles  Armstrong,  playing  with  Ward 
Burton,  won  a  four-set  match  from  Payne  and  Wheeler,  6/4,  5/7,  6/0,  6/3. 
The    summaries:

Arkansas  State  Championship. 

The  Little  Rock  Country  Club  was  again  the  scene  of  the  annual 
Arkansas  State  championship  and  September  25  was  the  date  of  the 
beginning  of  the  meeting.  Ralph  Payne  of  Texarkana  won  the  champion- 
ship in  singles,  when  he  defeated  Harry  Munz  in  the  linal  round  at  11/9, 
3/6,  6/0,  6/1.  Payne  played  splendidly  toward  the  end  of  the  match, 
serving  and  driving  with  remarkable  speed.  These  two  combined  in  the 
doubles  and  won  that  event  easily.  Alexander  and  Hannay  who  met 
them   in   the   final   match   were   outclassed   completely.      The    summaries:

Metropolitan  Championship 

^  In  a  meeting  which  was  remarkable  for  its  form  reversals  and  surpris- 
ing results,  Fred  C.  Inman  won  the  Metropolitan  Championship  for  the 
second  time  in  three  years,  in  191 1.  The  tournament  was  played,  as  usual, 
at  the  upper  .grounds  of  the  West  Side  Tennis  Club  of  New  York,  begin- 
ning June   17. 

Though  not  to  be  compared  in  class  with  the  same  event  of  a  year  ago, 
which  was  won  by  W.  A.  Larned,  there  were  a  number  of  good  men  in 
It,  including  the  winner,  Inman,  C.  R.  Gardner,  G.  F.  Touchard,  W.  M. 
Hall,  L.  E.  Mahan  and  K.  H.  Behr.  The  doubles  was  decidedly  better, 
and  had,  among  other  good  teams,  N.  W.  Niles  and  B.  C.  Wright  of 
Boston. 

The  luck  of  the  draw  brought  two  of  the  best  men  together  in  the  first 
round,  namely,  C.  R.  Gardner  and  G.  F.  Touchard.  Gardner  won  in  a 
match  which  was  noteworthy  only  for  its  length,  all  three  sets  going  to 
deuce.  A  decided  upset  occurred  in  the  same  round  when  G.  C.  Shafer 
eliminated  K.  H.  Behr.  The  latter  was  very  wild,  and  Shafer,  who  was 
steady  and   sure,   made   fewer   errors  by   half  than   his   famous   opponent 

The  next  surprising  feature  appeared  in  the  defeat  of  W.  M.  Washburn 
^j  i.  ^"  \oshell.  The  latter's  hard  hitting  swept  Washburn  off  his  feet 
and   he   made  a   poor   showing  against  the   Brooklyn   man. 

In  a  later  round  an  interesting  meeting  took  place  between  L.  E.  Mahan 
and  Inman.  Th-  gigantic  West  Sider  was  apparently  in  control  of  the 
situation  when  darkness  ended  play.  He  led  at  6/3  and  3/0,  but  the 
following  day  Inman  took  six  straight  games  and  the  deciding  set  later  at 
6/4.  He  was  much  improved,  while  in  Mahan's  case  the  interval  seemed 
to   have   thrown   him   way   off   his   game. 

Dean  Mathey  won  from  F.  Gates  after  dropping  the  first  set,  and 
Church  did  the  same  in  his  match  with  Dr.  E.  Taylor.  A.  S  Stillman 
won  from  Hugh  Tallant,  and  Shafer  made  short  work  of  C.  R.  Leonard, 
after  the  latter  had  defeated  H.  J.  Mollenhauer.  Two  veterans  met  when 
E.  P.  Fisher  and  C.  W.  Leonard  clashed,  but  Leonard  got  away  with  the 
deciding  set. 

Hall  sprung  a  surprise  in  the  fourth  round  by  putting  C.  R.  Gardner 
out  of  the  running,  but  failed  to  maintain  the  high  standard  he  set  for 
himself  by  losing  in  the  semi-final  to  Shafer.  The  latter  gained  his  place 
by  disposing  of  Church.  Inman  outclassed  Leonard  in  their  match,  and 
Mathey   coupled    with    him   by   smothering   Stillman. 

The  Inman-Mathey  set-to  was  one  of  the  best  of  the  week.  Inman 
struck  his  gait  first  and  ran  out  the  first  set  at  6-3.  Mathey  took  the 
second,  6/2,  but  the  third  was  Inman  all  the  way.  He  "hit  harder  and 
was  more   accurate,  and   Mathey   was   credited    with   but   one   game. 

The  final  between  Inman  and  Shafer  was  fast,  interesting  tennis  from 
beginning  to  end.  Inman  was  the  first  to  get  going  and  by  beautiful 
driving  took  two  sets  easily.  He  passed  Shafer  forehand  and  back- 
hand with  the  greatest  ease  and  for  the  time  being  outclassed  him  com- 
pletely. The  third  set  found  Shafer  getting  stronger,  while  Inman  seemed 
to  have  tired  from  his  early  efforts.  The  former  won  at  7/5,  but  it  was 
no  easy  task.  After  the  rest  Inman  appeared  greatly  refreshed,  and  play- 
ing perfect  tennis,  ran  out  the  fourth  set  at  love.  Shafer  never  had  a 
chance,   for  no  matter  what  he  attempted,  Inman  met  him  with   something 

The  doubles  produced  a  good  match  in  the  first  round,  when  Wright 
and  Niles  played  Mahan  and  Touchard.  The  latter  put  up  an  unexpectedly 
f-J^'^^rr^l^^^'  ^"^  ^fter  being  led  at  3/0  in  the  third  set,  ran  it  out  at 
6/4.      ihe  best  meeting,   however,   was  between  C.   R.   Gardner  and  H.   H. 


154  SPALDING'S   LAWN    TENNIS   ANNUAL. 

Hackett  and  W.  A.  and  E.  P.  Larned.  After  set-all  had  been  reached  the 
former,  by  brilliant  all-round  play,  got  to  5/0  and  40/0,  but  W.  A.  Larned, 
who  was  serving,  pulled  that  game  out  and  another  before  relinquishing 
his  chances.     The   score  was  3/6,   6/2.. 

The  winners  of  that  match  had  little  time  to  gloat  over  their  victory, 
however,  for  in  the  very  next  round  they  were  decisively  trounced  by 
Behr  and  Little.  Little  played  magnificently,  and  Behr,  too,  was  in  good 
form,  so  that  Hackett  and  Gardner,  who  were  a  shade  below  par,  made  a 
sorry  showing. 

In  the  upper  half  of  the  semi-final  Touchard  and  Mahan  had  hard  work 
in  defeating  O.  H.  Hinck  and  H.  Torrance,  but  Behr  and  Little,  after 
dropping  the  second  set  at  14/12,  took  the  deciding  one  at  6/2  from  W, 
Rosenbaum  and   B.   M.   Phillips. 

The  final  match  upset  calculations  by  going  to  Mahan  and  Touchard  in 
four  sets.  No  one  expected  them  to  win,  but  Mahan  was  a  tower  of 
strength  at  serving,  volleying  and  overhand,  while  Touchard  had  his  drives 
under  perfect  control.  The  score  was  6/3,  2/6,  7/5,  7/5-  The  summaries:

Niagara  Tournament 

The  twenty-fifth  annual  international  tournament  at  Niagara-on-the- 
Lake,  held  on  the  courts  of  the  Niagara  Tennis  Club  at  the  Queen's  Royal 
Hotel,  between  August  28  and  September  2,  was  remarkable  for  the 
appearance  of  the  two  sterling  women  champions.  Miss  Hazel  Hotchkiss 
and  Miss  May  Sutton.  They  met  in  the  tinal  round  of  the  women's  sin- 
gles, with  the  result  that  the  first  named  won,  after  losing  the  first  set, 
0/6,  by  coming  through  at  7/5  and  6/0.  E.  H.  Whitney  won  the  men's 
singles  from  F.  H.  Harris  in  five  sets,  and  Miss  Hotchkiss  and  Harris 
accounted  for  the  mixed  doubles,  winning  from  Miss  Florence  Sutton  and 
Baird.      The  summary:

Miscellaneous   Tournaments 


Chevy  Chase  Tournament. 

The  Chevy  Chase  Club,  with  its  beautiful  grounds  and  excellent  courts; 
held  its  fourth  annual  tournament  late  in  May.  But  for  all  its  attractive 
features  and  mid-season  weather,  which  one  finds  at  that  time  of  year  jn 
Washington,  the  event  did  not  draw  the  high  class  entry  of  former  years 
in  either  singles  or  doubles. 

C.  B.  Doyle,  far  the  fastest  man  developed  in  the  nation's  capital,  won 
the  singles  without  the  loss  of  a  set.  His  play  was  so  good  that  opinion 
favored  him  in  his  challenge  match  against  G.  F.  Touchard,  especially  after 
a  series  of  practice  games  between  the  two,  in  which  the  latter  was 
invariably  worsted.  However,  the  Washingtonian  was  found  wanting,  and 
alter  a  good  start  and  determined  fight  for  three  sets,  was  overwhelmed  in 
the   fourth.     The  score  in   Touchard's  favor   was   6/8,   8/6    7/5,   6/1. 

The  doubles  was  practically  a  present  to  the  famous  Doyle  brothers.  No 
one  approached  their  class  and  not  a  team  was  able  to  force  a  set  to 
deuce.  In  the  final,  E.  P.  Grosvenor  and  G.  P.  Parks  were  defeated.  6/1, 
6/2,  6/4.  The  victory  gave  the  brothers  permanent  possession  of  the  chal- 
lenge bowls,  for  the  defending  team,  W.  F,  Johnson  and  L.  E.  Mahan, 
were  not  on  hand.     The  summaries:

New  York  Tennis  Club  Tournament. 

One  of  the  handsomest  trophies  ever  presented  for  a  tennis  event  was 
captured  outright,  when  G.  F.  Touchard  won,  for  the  third  successive  year, 
the  New  York  Tennis  Club's  annual  spring  meeting.  There  was  a  fair 
entry  in  both  singles  and  doubles,  but  the  defending  players  in  both  were 
the  strongest.  W.  M.  Hall  won  the  tournament.  He  surprised  everyone 
by  defeating  T.  R.  Pell  in  the  final  in  most  convincing  style.  Pell  never 
had  a  real  chance,  and  Hall  won  at  8/6,  6/0,  6/1.  Hall  made  a  strong 
fight  in  the  challenge  round.  He  won  the  first  and  third  sets,  but  fell  off 
badly   in  the   fifrh.      The   complete   score   was:   4/6,   7/5,   6/3,   4/6,    6/2. 


160  SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL. 

Hackett  and  Alexander  clinched  the  hold  on  the  bowls,  which  represent 
the  championship  of  Manhattan,  by  again  wading  through  the  field  in 
hollow  style.  It  was  their  third  victory  of  the  kind,  and  so  the  club  suf- 
fered the  final  loss  of  two  more  challenge  trophies.  Pell  and  Mahan  were 
the  only  other  high  class  combination  to  enter.  The  latter  won  the  open- 
ing set.  but  thereafter  the  national  champions  had  matters  much  their  own 
way.     The  summaries:

Harlem's  Annual  Meeting. 

The  first  tournament  to  be  played  in  New  York  for  the  191 1  season  v/as 
that  held  by  the  Harlem  Club.  It  began  on  May  11,  and  brought  out  a 
number  of  well  known  players  of  the  Metropolitan  district.  Among  them 
were  W.  C.  Grant,  B.  M.  Phillips,  Dr.  W.  Rosenbaum  and  L.  Leventritt. 
Phillips  and  Grant  came  together  in  the  final  and  Phillips  won.  He  was 
more  aggressive  and  infinitely  steadier  than  his  tall  rival,  and  after  a  bad 
start  set  sail  in  a  way  that  left  Grant  but  little  chance.  Phillips  won  at 
0/6,  6/4,  6/2,   1 1/9. 

Grant  and  Phillips  won  the  doubles,  defeating  A.  D.  Hammatt  and 
Rosenbaum  in   the   final.  

West  Virginia  Open  Tournament. 

The  second  annual  open  tennis  tournament  of  the  Edgewood  Country 
Club  of  Charleston,  W.  \'a.,  was  held  on  the  club's  clay  courts,  September 
25  to  28.  S.  Jarvis  Adams,  Jr.,  of  Pittsburgh,  won  the  singles,  with  J.  S. 
Dana  of  Charleston  the  runner-up.  The  double  event  was  captured  by 
Adams  and  Vinton  of  Johnstown,  Pa.  The  State  championship  ^yere  the 
titles   involved.      The   summary:

Central  California  Championship. 

The  first  meeting  for  191 1  of  the  famous  San  Franciscans,  M.  E. 
McLoughlin  and  M.  H.  Long,  occurred  at  the  end  of  the  newly  created 
Central  California  championship,  held  in  May  by  the  Stockton  Tennis  Club 
of  Stockton,  Cal. 

Neither  man  lost  a  set  on  his  way  through  to  the  finals,  but  the  final 
match  was  as  one-sided  as  the  contestants'  earlier  victories  had  been.  Long 
was  short  of  practice  and  utterly  without  control.  McLoughlin,  on  the 
other  hand,   was  at   his  best  and   won  easily  at   6/2,  6/2,   7/5. 

Long  and  McLoughlin  as  a  team  were  too  fast  for  the  rest  of  the  field 
and  won  the  doubles  easily.  With  Miss  Hotchkiss,  McLoughlin  scored 
his  third  victory  in  the  mixed.     The  summaries:

Metropolitan  Women's  Championship. 

In  the  Metropolitan  women's  championships,  decided  in  New  York,  Miss 
Hazel  Hotchkiss  was  the  star  player  of  the  tournament,  as  she  defeated 
Mrs.  Wallach  in  the  singles  by  6/0,  6/1,  and  later  on,  with  Carlton  R. 
Gardner  as  a  partner,  was  instrumental  in  accounting  for  the  mixed  dou- 
bles when  they  defeated  Mrs.  Chapman  and  Artemus  Holmes  in  straight 
sets.  Still  further  along  in  the  series,  with  Miss  Browning  as  a  partner. 
Miss  Hotchkiss  was  a  victor  in  the  women's  doubles,  when  Miss  Sutton 
and  Miss  Green  were  defeated,  3/6,  6/2,  6/1.  The  consolation  singles- 
was  won  by  Miss  Elizabeth  Bunce  over  Miss  Clara  Kuttroff  by  6/2,  6/2. 
The   summaries:

Miss  Marie  Wagner  a  Winner. 

Miss  Marie  Wagner,  the  indoor  champion  of  1910-1911,  won  the  second 
annual  open  tournament  held  on  the  courts  of  the  Montclair  (N.  J.)  Ath- 
letic Club  when  she  defeated  Miss  Gwendolyn  Rees,  former  Minnesota 
State  champion,  in  a  three-set  match.  The  doubles  were  won  by  Mis3 
Elizabeth  Moore  and  Mrs.  R.  B.  Neff,  who  defeated  Miss  Wagner  and 
Miss  Clara  Kuttroff  in  the  final  round  by  6/4,  6/4.     The  summary:

Southern  Pennsylvania  Championships. 

The    Southern    Pennsylvania   championship    was   decided   on   the  courts   of 

the    Bedford    Springs    (Pa.)    Tennis    Club,    August    19.      In    the  challenge 

round   of   the   singles   P.    D.    Siverd   defeated   H.    J.    Rendall.    6/0,  6/3,    6/3, 

and    later.    Siverd    playing   with    Cote,    annexed    the    doubles    title,  defeating 
the  Rendalls.     The  summary:

Miss  Hotchkiss  Stars  at  Longwood. 

The  annual  tournament  for  women,  held  at  the  Longwood  Cricket  Club, 
Boston,  in  September,  showed  to  advantage  the  playing  of  Miss  Hazel 
Hotchkiss  of  California,  who  went  through  to  the  final  round,  where  she 
met  and  defeated  Miss  Edith  Rotch  of  Boston,  6/2,  6/0.  In  the  doubles, 
paired  with  Miss  Eleanora  Sears,  who  did  her  share  of  the  work  in 
acceptable  style,  she  won  again,  defeating  Mrs.  Barger-Wallach  and  Miss 
Rotch  in  straight  sets,  while  later  on,  with  E.  H.  Whitney  as  a  partner, 
Miss  Hotchkiss  accounted  for  the  mixed  doubles.  They  defeated  Mrs. 
Wallach  and  H.  C.  Johnson  in  two  sets,  the  score  being  6/2,  8/6.  The 
summary :

Miss  May  Sayres  won  the  singles  championship  for  women  of  Philadel- 
phia and  district  on  the  courts  of  the  Merion  Cricket  Club,  September  16, 
from  a  field  of  thirty-one.  The  tournament  was  robbed  of  some  of  its 
interest  through  the  illness  of  Miss  Anna  Wallace,  the  title  holder  of 
1910,  who  was  unable  to  defend.     In  the  final  round  Miss  Sayres  defeated

Miss  May  Sutton  Wins  at  Syracuse. 

The  invitation  mixed  doubles  tournament  held  on  the  Onondaga  Country 
Club  courts,  Syracuse,  September  11,  12  and  13.  resulted  in  a  victorv  for 
Miss  May  Sutton  and  Harry  Kirkover.  Miss  Florence  Sutton  and  A.  H. 
Lewis  were  the  victims  in  the  closest  kind  of  a  match.  There  were  twelve 
teams  in  the  series  and  interest  centered  in  the  work  of  the  Sutton  sisters.

Central  Iowa  Tennis  Association  Tournament. 

The  sixth  annual  meet  of  the  Central  Iowa  Tennis  Association  was  held 
on  its  home  courts  at  Toledo,  Iowa,  July  11 -15.  A  number  of  states  were 
represented  and  the  only  regret  for  Iowa  was  the  fact  that  in  the  persons 
of  John  Barton  and  George  Douthit,  both  of  Sioux  Falls,  S.  D.,  that  State 
•was  enabled  to  carry  off  our  trophies,  both  in  singles  and  doubles;  but 
defeat  only  tends  to  greater  effort,  and  the  1912  tournament  already  prom- 
ises great  things  in   tennis  for  the   Central   Iowa   Tennis  Association. 

"Who's  Who"  in  Iowa  tennis  is  shown  annually  in  the  Central  Iowa  at 
Toledo.   The  summaries:

New  Haven  Tournament. 

One  of  R.  A.  Holden's  wins  during  the  191  r  season  was  the  New  Haven 
Lawn  Club  event,  which  was  played  early  in  June.  Professor  G.  H. 
Nettleton,  who  challenged  Holden,  was  routed  ingloriously  and  failed  to 
make  much  of  a  fight.  Holden  took  the  cup  away  from  Nettleton  in  1910 
and  it  was  predicted  that  the  Professor  would  retaliate  by  doing  likewise 
to  his  student.  Holden,  however,  showed  none  of  the  respect  that  might 
characterize  his  actions  under  different  circumstances  and  trounced  his 
dispenser  of  knowledge  at  6/3,  6/1,  6/3.  Nettleton  had  better  luck  in  the 
doubles.  Paired  with  Z.  Sargent  he  won  from  Man  and  Wainwright  in 
the  final  at   7/9,   3/6,   6/4,   6/4,   6/2.      I 


Bronxville  Tournament. 

G.  F.  Touchard  came  within  one  point  of  losing  his  match  with  G.  M. 
Church  in  the  challenge  round  of  the  Bronxville  tournament,  which  was 
played  the  week  beginning  July  3.  The  Princeton  freshman  waded 
through  a  big  field  of  ninety-two  players  without  the  loss  of  a  set  and 
for  a  time  played  Touchard  to  a  standstill  in  the  challenge  round.  He  led 
at  2  sets  to  I  and  was  within  a  point  of  the  match,  when  an  unlucky 
smash  gave  his  older  rival  a  chance.  The  flubbing  of  that  single  shot 
upset  the  young  Tiger  crack  for  several  points  following,  and  he  was 
never    within   striking    distance    after   that. 

Church,  playing  with  W.  Blache,  won  the  doubles  easily,  and  Touchard, 
with  Miss  Emeline  W.  Holmes  for  a  partner,  got  away  with  the  mixed 
event. 


Long  Island  Championship. 

Once  a  Mecca  for  the  strongest  players  of  the  Metropolitan  district,  the 
old  Kings  County  Club,  where  the  championship  of  Long  Island  is  annually 
played  for,  no  longer  attracts  the  elect  in  tennis.  On  June  26  the  yearly 
meeting  began,  but  it  proved  a  runaway  for  G.  F.  Touchard.  The  New 
Yorker  won  hands  down,  and  in  the  challenge  round  took  the  measure  of 
W.  B.  Cragin,  Jr.  The  match  went  the  full  five  sets,  but  in  the  fifth 
Cragin   was   outclassed  and  failed  to  win  a  game. 

Just  as  easy  as  Touchard's  victory  in  the  singles  had  been  was  the 
doubles  for  Bull  and  Martin.  The  Crescent  pair  met  the  Gates  Brothers 
of  Yale  in  the  final  and  defeated  them  without  an  effort  at  6/2,  6/0,  6/1. 
The   summaries:

Ardsley  Open  Tournament. 

Ardsley,  one  of  the  first  grass  court  events  of  the  season,  brought  out 
quite  a  strong  field  and  also  some  unimpressive  reversals  of  form.  The 
singles  included  G.  F.  Touchard,  K.  H.  Behr,  E.  P.  Earned,  F.  C.  Inman 
and  other  well-known  men.  but  Touchard  and  Earned  defaulted  and  Behr 
was  defeated  by  R.  A.  Holden,  Jr.,  in  the  semi-final.  The  final  round 
brought  together  Inman  and  Holden,  but  the  ex-Yale  captain  was  in  form 
far  in  advance  ot  the  season  and  Inman  was  trounced  at  6/3,   6/3,    6/2.

the   final  at  6/3,   6/3,   6/2.     The   summaries:

Bronx  Championship. 


G.  F.  Touchard  won  the  first  tournament  to  be  played  in  the  vicinity 
of  New  York  for  the  season  of  191 1  when  he  regained  the  honors  lost  to 
C.  R.  Gardner  a  year  ago  in  the  Bedford  Park  tournament  on  May  28. 
Touchard  met  S.  H.  Voshell  in  the  final  and  defeated  him  in  four  sets. 
The    challenge    round    between    Gardner   and    Touchard    was    played    under

adverse    conditions,    which    afifected    Gardner's    game    much    more    than    the 
former's.      Reimer  and   Roberts   won  the   doubles.      The  summaries:

Tennis  at  Pinehurst. 

On  January  29,  191 1,  the  annual  midwinter  tournament  at  Pinehurst 
began  at  the  Pinehurst  Country  Club  and  as  usual  attracted  a  number  ot 
well-known  players.  Among  these  were  R.  D.  Little  of  New  York,  Richard 
Bishop  of  Boston  and  R.  L.  James  of  Saratoga  Springs,  N.  Y.  The 
women,  however,  were  on  hand  in  greater  numbers  and  included  such 
experts  as  Miss  Edna  Wildey,  Mrs.  George  L.  Chapman,  Mrs.  A.  G.  Miles, 
Mrs.   Marshall    McLean  and   Miss   Elsie    Little. 

In  the  men's  singles  Bishop  and  Little  outclassed  the  rest  of  the  field 
and.  having  been  on  opposite  sides  of  the  draw,  came  together  in  the  final. 
The   result   was  a  long  five-set  match,   which   Little  finally  pulled   out.      The 


SPALDING'S    LAWN    TENNIS    ANNUAL,  177 

fifth  set  went  to  7/5.  The  women's  singles  was  won  by  Mrs.  McLean 
who  defeated  Miss  Edna  Wildey  in  the  final,  6/1,  3/6,  6/1.  Miss  Little 
and  her  brother,  R.  D.  Little,  came  out  on  top  in  the  mixed  event,  while 
the  women's  doubles  winners  were  Miss  Little  and  Miss  Wildey.  The 
summaries; 

MEN'S  SINGLES. 

First  round — S.  W.  Merrihew  (Plainfield)  d.  Charles  Banes  (Marion 
CO,  6/1,  6/2;  R.  D.  Little  (West  Side  T.C.)  d.  R.  Durant  (Alaska), 
6/2,  6/3;  Richard  Bishop  (Longwood  C.C.)  d.  T.  H.  Hall  (Toronto),  6/0, 
6/2;  R.  L.  James  (Belmont  C.C.)  d.  H.  D.  Kirkover  (Park  Club),  by 
default. 

Second  round — Walter  Goldstein  (Toronto)  d.  R.  C.  King  (New 
Canaan),  by  default;  Little  d.  Merrihew,  6/2,  6/1;  Bishop  d.  James,  6/4, 
5/7,  6/1;  Herbert  Coppell  (Englewood)  d.  George  Chapman  (Nyack), 
6/4,  6/1.

Metropolitan  League. 


The  Metropolitan  League  of  New  York  City  and  District  regained  con- 
siderable prestige  last  fall  by  putting  through  its  annual  schedule  of  inter- 
club  matches  without  any  great  accidents  happening  to  mar  the  tourna- 
ment. In  19 10  the  schedule  was  dragged  along  through  summer  and  fall 
till  there  was  little  left  but  tatters  and  no  result  was  obtained.  In  191 1, 
however,  the  month  of  September  was  chosen  for  the  play  and  the  affair 
came  promptly  to  a  definite  conclusion  on  September  30,  the  New  York 
Lawn  Tennis  Club  capturing  first  place  by  a  4  to  i  victory  over  the 
Montclair   Athletic  Club.     The   summaries:

Seabri^ht   Tournament 

The  performance  of  M.  H.  Long  in  coming  from  California  and  begin- 
ning on  the  same  day  he  arrived,  July  lo,  to  play  in  the  Seabright  tour- 
nament, his  first  grass  court  effoits  in  over  a  year  and  a  half,  was  remark- 
able for  the  fact  of  his  plural  success.  Long  not  only  won  the  singles, 
defeating  Niles  in  the  challenge  round,  but  the  doubles  as  well,  with  his 
one-time  team-mate,   C.   R.   Gardner,   for  a   partner. 

Long  defeated  in  succession  E.  P.  Larned,  G.  M.  Church,  A.  S.  Dabney, 
R.  R.  Pell  and  N.  W.  Niles.  His  first  match,  against  Larned,  was  won 
in  straight  sets  at  6/3  and  6/4.  Church  did  better,  winning  the  opening 
set  at  6/4,  but  dropping  the  third  and  fourth,  6/3.  6/2.  Dabney,  who  had 
previously  eliininated  Touchard,  was  outclassed,  winning  but  two  games  in 
each  set.' 

The  final,  against  Pell,  was  a  four-set  affair,  which  Long  held  safe  after 
the  first  set,  but  Niles  made  a  stronger  stand  when  they  faced  each  other 
in  the  challenge  match.  Five  sets  were  played  and  throughout  there  was 
little  advantage  gained  on  either  side.  A  flying  start  in  the  fifth  set  of 
four  games  to  none  practically  ended  the  match,  for  although  Niles  braced 
well  and  succeeded  in  getting  to  3/4  and  4/5,  Long  took  the  tenth  game 
with  his  own  delivery,  and  the  match. 

His  win  gave  him  a  leg  on  the  famous  Achilles  Cup,  which  is  now  the 
best  from  the  standpoint  of  sentiment,  in  America.  The  names  of  W.  A. 
Larned.  B.  C.  Wright,  F.  B.  Alexander,  W.  J.  Clothier,  R.  D.  Little,  N. 
W.  Niles  and  M.  H.  Long  are  now  engraved  on  it,  and  its  value  as  a 
trophy   still   in   competition  is   without   a   parallel. 

There  were  a  number  of  good  teams  in  the  doubles,  which  finally  sim- 
mered down  to  the  Larned  brothers  and  Long  and  Gardner.  The  final 
was  played  on   Saturday  before   the   largest  crowd   of  the   week. 

For  two  sets  the  Californians  had  it  all  their  own  way,  but  after  drop- 
ping the  first  four  games  of  the  third  set,  they  made  no  effort  to  even  up, 
allowing  it  to  go  at  love.  The  fourth  was  theirs  at  6/2.  By  taking  the 
net  and  volleying  and  smashing  perfectly,  they  had  the  brothers  on  the 
defensive  continuously  and  without  a  chance  to  get  aggressive,  point- 
winning  plays  in  action.     The  summaries:

Larned  d.  L.  E.  Mahan,  6/4,  6/0;  M.  H.  .Long  d,  E.  P.  Larned,  6/3,  6/4; 
G.  M.  Church  d.  K.  H.  Behr,  6/4,  6/4.

SPALDING'S    LAWN     TENNIS    ANNUAL. 


The  English  Championships 

Early  in  July  the  annual  English  championship  was  played  at  the  All 
England    Lawn   Tennis   and    Croquet   Club    of   Wimbledon. 

Entries  were  received  from  every  important  tennis  playmg  county  of 
the  world — America,  France,  Canada.  Australia,  Germany,  Portugal, 
Sweden,  Denmark,  Belgium  and  New  Zealand  all  had  representatives  in 
the  field  and,  with  the  exception  of  America,  the  men  from  foreign  coun- 
tries  were   the    strongest   that  could   have   been    sent. 

As  it  has  always  been  in  England,  the  big  annual  fixture  attracted  atten- 
tion which  in  America  and  other  lands  would  be  focused  only  on  racing, 
foot  ball  or  some  other  sporting  event.  Tennis  there  ranks  with  the  lead- 
ing  sports   and    interest   from    all    classes   is   invariably    manifested. 

First  round  results  were  unimportant,  saving  the  unexpected  defeat  of 
the  German,  H.  Kleinschroth,  by  the  veteran  T.  M.  Mavrogordato,  and 
H.   Roper  Barrett's   easy    win   over   J.   C     Parke. 

The  second  session  produced  a  big  sensation  when  young  A.  H.  Gobert. 
the  French  champion,  who  had  taken  Europe  by  storm  with  his  remarkable, 
though  erratic,  performances,  went  down  in  straight  sets  to  the  ex-English 
champion,  Gore.  Tlie  latter's  driving  was  too  fast  and  accurate  for  the 
youthful  son  of  France  and  he  "blew  up"  before  the  match  was  well 
under    way. 

The  meeting  of  the  brothers  Lowe  was  the  feature  of  the  third  round, 
but  after  F.   G.   had  secured  a   lead   of  two   sets  to   one     A.   H.   defaulted. 

The  fourth  had  but  few  of  the  weaker  entrants  left.  C.  P.  Dixon 
eliminated  M.  T-  G.  Ritchie  m  tour  close  sets  and  Max  Decugis  put  Gore 
out  of  the  running  with  a  similar  number.  Roper  Barrett  upset  Mavro- 
gordato at  6/3,  3/6,  8/6,  8/6.  and  Rahe.  another  German  ot  great  ability, 
defeated   de    Borenau   in   straight    sets. 

The  fifth  round  resulted  in  the  hnai  appearance  of  Rod  Heath  of  Aus- 
tralia, Thomas,  Beamish  and  Rahe.  Decugis  accounted  for  the  first  named 
and  Dixon  did  for  Thomas.  Beamish  was  outplayed  by  Barret*-  and  Rahe 
struggled    vainly    against    Lowe's   accurate    baseline    game. 

Decugis  met  Dixon  in  the  upper  half  of  the  semi-final  and  Barrett  faced 
Lowe   in   the  lower. 

France's  chance  of  representation  was  snuffed  by  Dixon  in  four  sets. 
Decugis  won  the  second  at  7/5.  but  the  other  three  were  easy  for  the 
Britisher. 

In  the  lower  half  Barrett  played  all  around  Lowe.  The  younger  man 
was  outgeneraled  from  the  first  point  to  the  last  and  never  had  a  real 
chance.      Barrett    won,   6/2,    6/3,   6/2. 

The  final  round  between  Dixon  and  Barrett,  was  one  of  the  features 
of  the  week.  Played  in  excessive  heat,  the  former  was  apparently  net 
affected  at  all  and  won  the  first  two  sets  handily  It  looked  then  as 
though  Barrett  was  done  for,  but  a  remarkable  recovery  and  the  winning 
of  three  successive  sets  for  the  match  was  the  amazing  accomplishment 
which  he  displayed.  Certainly  Dixon  should  have  won  it  but  lapses  into 
indifferent  play,  for  which  he  is  noted,  cost  him  many  opportunities,  never 
so  pronounced  as  on  this  occasion  when  the  championship  seemed  within 
his  grasp. 

The  greatest  disappointment  was  felt  at  the  result  of  the  challenge 
match  between  Wilding,  the  title  holder,  and  Barrett.  The  latter  was  so 
unfortunate  as  to  suffer  with  illness  the  night  before  and  he  came  upon 
the  court  the  following  day  absolutely  unfit  for  the  contest  before  him. 
Wilding  took  the  first  set.  6/4,  and  then  proceeded  to  go  completely  off 
his  game.      Barrett  played    softly,    but  with   telling  steadiness,   and  the   hard 


1,  H.  r\  Wilding,  Champion  of   England;    2,  H.  Roper- Barrett,  Winner  English 
All-Comers'  Tournament.

hitting  New  Zealander,  who  can  do  his  best  only  against  an  opponent  who 
plays  with  equal  speed;  whanged  away  at  the  net  and  backstop  and  totaled 
numberless   errors. 

The  fourth  set,  however,  was  Wilding's  easily  by  virtue  of  Barrett's 
■wretched  physical  condition.  The  latter  played  only  by  tremendous  force 
of  will,  but  even  his  determination  failed  him,  for  his  condition  was  such 
at  the  beginning  of  his   set  that   he   was   compelled   to   drop   out. 

The  doubles  fell  to  Gobert  and  Decugis.  They  defeated  Parke  and 
Hardy,  the  Americans,  in  straight  sets  in  the  tinal  round.  The  losers 
were   outclassed,   as   the   score    of   6/2,   6/1.   6/2,   shows  only   too    plainly. 

In  the  challenge  round  Gobert  and  Decugis  upset  calculations  by  defeat- 
ing the  title  holders.  Wilding  and  M.  J.  G.  Ritchie  in  a  fast,  interesting 
iive-set  affair. 

The  ladies'  championship  was  retained  by  Mrs.  Lambert  Chambers,  her 
challenger.  Miss  Dorothy  Boothby,  failing  to  score  a  single  game  against 
her.      The   summaries:

SPALDING'S     LAWN     TENNIS     ANNUAL.  187 


Tournament  Notes 


Siwanoy  Country  Club  Tournament. — Abraham  Bassford,  Jr.,  president  of 
the  famous  Chimney  Club,  captured  the  open  tournament  of  the  Siwanoy 
Country  Club  of  Mount  V'ernon.  N.  Y.,  on  July  15.  The  victor  experienced 
some  very  hard  rounds  on  his  way  through  the  field.  In  the  third  round  he 
was  forced  to  his  best  by  C.  Major,  the  score  being  8/6,  4/6,  6/4,  and  again 
in  the  following  round  A.  Behr  carried  him  at  a  pace  which  required  the 
playing  of  a  third  set.  In  the  semi-final  he  lowered  the  colors  of  Dr.  Rosen- 
baum  at  6/1,  6/2,  much  to  the  surprise  of  everyone,  and  in  the  final  tilt  he 
was  victorious  over  A.  H.  Hammett  in  straight  sets  at  6/3,  6/4,  6/2.  Major 
and  Johnson  captured  the  doubles  by  defeating  Rosenbaum  and  Hammett  in 
the   final  at   6/1,   6/3,    6/4. 

Falls  City  Championship. — Lewis  Hardy  of  Memphis  successfully  defended 
his  title  against  Wallace  Frank  in  the  fourth  annual  championship  of  the 
Falls  City  Club  on  the  clay  courts  in  Central  Park,  Louisville,  Ky.,  July  1.5. 
In  the  final  round  Frank  was  successful  over  S.  Arterburn,  6/4,  8/6,  2/6, 
8/6.  6/3.  In  the  challenge  round  Hardy  was  called  upon  by  Frank  to  defend 
his  title,  which  he  accomplished  in  three  sets.  The  Arterburn  brothers,  who 
were  picked  to  win  the  doubles,  did  not  disappoint  their  followers.  They 
defeated   Barfield  and   Frank,   6/3,   6/2,   9/7. 

Westfall's  Lancaster  Trophy. — H.  L.  Westfall  captured  the  Lancaster  trophy 
at  the  Edgenieve  Tennis  Club,  L.  I.,  on  August  6  by  defeating  W.  A.  Camp- 
bell in  the  final  at  8/6,  6/3,  6/1.  Westfall  showed  a  vestige  of  the  form 
that  made  him  a  formidable  expert  three  or  four  years  ago,  and  at  times 
completely   outplayed  the   Crescent   club   man. 

Mount  Washington  Tournament. — At  the  annual  open  tournament  of  the 
Mount  Washington  Club,  one  of  the  most  active  tennis  organizations  around 
Baltimore,  held  in  July,  Harry  Davis  carried  oft"  the  honors  in  the  singles  by 
defeating  C.  S.  Brooke  in  the  best  of  five  sets  at  7/5.  2/6.  6/2,  3/6.  12/10. 
McLanahan  and  Donaldson  defeated  Ensor  and  Whitehurst  in  the  doubles  in 
straight  sets,    7/5,    6/4,    6/2. 

Doughty's  Detroit  Honors. — Richard  H.  Doughty  won  the  Detroit  champion- 
ship in  the  biggest  tournament  ever  held  in  the  state  of  Michigan,  which  was 
completed  in  Detroit,  July  13.  His  opponent  in  the  challenge  round  was  J. 
L.  Hibbard,  whom  he  defeated,  6/1,  6/1,  6/2.  The  summaries:  Class  A  sin- 
gless:  First  round — F.  H.  Gill  d.  L.  A.  Murray,  6/0.  6/1;  Theodore  Lightner

University  Heights  (N.  Y.)  Tournament. — The  annual  open  tournament  of

■r  30.  The  draw  included  many  prominent  players  of  the  Metropolitan  dis-
